enters the \(3N\) regime (\(\eta < 0\)).

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{appendix-v---rowlands-petit-two-faces-of-the-same-pentadic-coin}{%
\subsection{Appendix V - Rowlands ↔ Petit: Two Faces of the Same
Pentadic
Coin}\label{appendix-v---rowlands-petit-two-faces-of-the-same-pentadic-coin}}

\hypertarget{v.1.-common-origin-the-pentadic-master-equation}{%
\subsubsection{V.1. Common origin: the pentadic master
equation}\label{v.1.-common-origin-the-pentadic-master-equation}}

The formalisms of Rowlands (algebraic microphysics) and Petit (bimetric
cosmology) are not independent theories but two distinct limits of a
single fundamental quantum equation governing the evolution of the
universal state in the pentadic Hilbert space
\(\mathcal{H}_{\text{Pent}}\):

\[
i\hbar \frac{\partial}{\partial t} |\Psi(t)\rangle = \hat{H}_{\text{total}} |\Psi(t)\rangle,
\]

with the total Hamiltonian decomposed into three contributions intrinsic
to the \(\text{Cl}(6,6)\) network:

\[
\hat{H}_{\text{total}} = \underbrace{\sum_P m_P |P\rangle\langle P| \otimes \mathbb{1}_{\text{st}}}_{\hat{H}_0 \text{ (mass terms)}} 
+ \underbrace{\sum_{P,Q,R,S} T^{RS}_{PQ} (|P\rangle\langle Q|) \otimes (|R\rangle\langle S|)}_{\hat{H}_{\text{int}} \text{ (interactions)}} 
+ \underbrace{\sum_{P^+,P^-} \mu_{P^+P^-} (|P^+\rangle\langle P^-| + \text{h.c.}) \otimes \mathbb{1}_{\text{st}}}_{\hat{H}_{\text{coupling}} \text{ (bicosmic coupling)}}.
\]

The Hilbert space naturally decomposes into a direct sum of the two
cosmos: \[
\mathcal{H}_{\text{Pent}} = \mathcal{H}^+_{\text{Pent}} \oplus \mathcal{H}^-_{\text{Pent}} \quad \Rightarrow \quad |\Psi\rangle = |\Psi^+\rangle + |\Psi^-\rangle.
\]

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Rowlands' viewpoint}: Project the master equation onto the
  discrete subspace \(\mathcal{H}^+_{\text{Pent}}\) and retain the full
  quantum dynamics. The eigenstates satisfy the nilpotent closure
  \((g\cdot x)^2=0\), giving rise to spin-½, native Pauli exclusion, and
  an active vacuum. The formalism remains purely algebraic and discrete.
\item
  \textbf{Petit's viewpoint}: Take the classical limit (\(\hbar \to 0\))
  and describe operators by effective continuous fields \(\Phi^\pm(x)\).
  The coupling term \(\hat{H}_{\text{coupling}}\) becomes a geometric
  interaction between two metrics \(g_{\mu\nu}^+\) and \(g_{\mu\nu}^-\).
  The coupled field equations of Janus cosmology are recovered.
\end{itemize}

Thus, Rowlands and Petit respectively describe the \textbf{quantum
microscopic limit} and the \textbf{classical macroscopic limit} of the
same master equation.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{v.2.-rowlands-petit-macroscopisation-via-coarse-graining}{%
\subsubsection{V.2. Rowlands → Petit: macroscopisation via
coarse-graining}\label{v.2.-rowlands-petit-macroscopisation-via-coarse-graining}}

The transition from Rowlands' discrete formalism to Petit's continuous
geometry is achieved via a \emph{coarse-graining} map \(\mathcal{C}\)
that averages pentadic states over macroscopic volumes:

\[
\mathcal{C} : \mathcal{H}_P \to L^2(\mathcal{M}_4), \quad \mathcal{C}(|P_\alpha\rangle) = \psi_\alpha(x) \xrightarrow[\text{classical}]{} \Phi^\pm(x).
\]

The transition operator \(T\), responsible for microscopic angular
rearrangements, has its macroscopic expectation value
\(\langle T \rangle_{\text{macro}}\) generate the effective
stress-energy tensors:

\[
T_{\mu\nu}^\pm(x) \sim \sum_{F \in CP/CN} \omega_F \, \text{Tr}\!\left( \Pi_F^\dagger \sigma_{\mu\nu}^\pm \Pi_F \right) \xrightarrow{\mathcal{C}} \langle T \rangle_{\text{macro}}^\pm.
\]

Projecting the master equation onto the classical fields \(\Phi^\pm\)
and retaining only the dominant terms (mass and self-interaction) yields
the coupled system:

\[
\Box \Phi^+ + m_+^2 \Phi^+ = \lambda (\Phi^+ \cdot \Phi^+) + \mu (\Phi^- \cdot \Phi^-),
\] \[
\Box \Phi^- + m_-^2 \Phi^- = \lambda (\Phi^- \cdot \Phi^-) + \mu (\Phi^+ \cdot \Phi^+).
\]

In bimetric general relativity, these source fields couple the
curvatures of the two metrics via generalized Bianchi identities,
leading directly to Janus' equations:

\[
R_{\mu\nu}^+ - \frac{1}{2}g_{\mu\nu}^+ R^+ = \frac{8\pi G}{c^4}\left( T_{\mu\nu}^+ + T_{\mu\nu}^- \right),
\] \[
R_{\mu\nu}^- - \frac{1}{2}g_{\mu\nu}^- R^- = \frac{8\pi G}{c^4}\left( T_{\mu\nu}^- + T_{\mu\nu}^+ \right).
\]

Janus cosmology thus emerges naturally as the macroscopic limit of the
coarse-grained pentadic dynamics.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{v.3.-petit-rowlands-microscopisation-via-spectral-decomposition}{%
\subsubsection{V.3. Petit → Rowlands: microscopisation via spectral
decomposition}\label{v.3.-petit-rowlands-microscopisation-via-spectral-decomposition}}

The inverse path consists of decomposing the macroscopic stress-energy
tensors onto the eigenbasis of the operator \(T\), whose spectrum is
fixed by the geometry of the \(\Lambda_{72}\) lattice. Starting from the
Janus equations in vacuum with the correct coupling terms:

\[
R_{\mu\nu}^+ - \frac{1}{2}R^+ g_{\mu\nu}^+ = \chi \left( T_{\mu\nu}^+ + \sqrt{\frac{g^-}{g^+}} \, T_{\mu\nu}^- \right),
\]

\[
R_{\mu\nu}^- - \frac{1}{2}R^- g_{\mu\nu}^- = -\chi \left( T_{\mu\nu}^- + \sqrt{\frac{g^+}{g^-}} \, T_{\mu\nu}^+ \right),
\]

where \(\chi = 8\pi G/c^4\) and \(g^\pm = |\det(g_{\mu\nu}^\pm)|\).

The stress-energy tensors admit a spectral decomposition arising from
the discrete lattice:

\[
T_{\mu\nu}^\pm(x) = \sum_{i=1}^{72} \alpha_i^\pm(x) \, \mathbf{W}_{i,\mu} \mathbf{W}_{i,\nu},
\]

where \(\mathbf{W}_{i,\mu}\) are the row vectors of the projection
matrix \(\mathbf{W} \in \mathbb{R}^{144 \times 10}\). The factors
\(\sqrt{g^\mp/g^\pm}\) ensure that the Bianchi identities
\(\nabla_\mu^\pm (T^{\mu\nu}_\pm + \sqrt{g^\mp/g^\pm} T^{\mu\nu}_\mp) = 0\)
are satisfied identically. Substituting into the Janus equations and
projecting onto the eigenvectors of \(T\) yields:

\[
\sum_j \left( \delta_{ij} \Box + M_{ij}^2 \right) \alpha_j^\pm(x) = \lambda \sum_{k,l} C_{ikl} \alpha_k^+ \alpha_l^- \pm \mu (\alpha^\pm)^3 + \text{volume terms}.
\]

The stationary solutions satisfy \((\lambda_n - m_n^2)\alpha_n = 0\).
For each eigenmode \(|\phi_n\rangle\) with \(\lambda_n \neq 0\), the
associated pentadic configuration satisfies \((g\cdot x)^2 = 0\),
recovering Rowlands' nilpotent states. The \(\pm\) sign in the cubic
term reflects the fundamental asymmetry between the two cosmos encoded
in the Janus equations.

For each eigenmode \(|\phi_n\rangle\) with \(\lambda_n \neq 0\), the
associated pentadic configuration satisfies by construction the
algebraic closure condition:

\[
(g \cdot x)^2 = 0,
\]

which is precisely the definition of Rowlands' nilpotent states. This
return to the microscopic level is formalized by the \emph{inverse
quantization} map \(\mathcal{Q}^{-1}\):

\[
\mathcal{Q}^{-1} : T_{\mu\nu}^\pm \mapsto |P\rangle \in \mathcal{H}_P, \quad \text{such that } \langle P | T | P \rangle = \int T_{\mu\nu}^\pm \, d^3x.
\]

Thus, nilpotent pentads emerge as the fundamental stationary modes of
the macroscopic bimetric field. Rowlands and Petit are therefore not in
competition; they describe the two faces of the same dual invariant,
connected by the reciprocal maps \(\mathcal{C}\) and
\(\mathcal{Q}^{-1}\).

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{appendix-w-primordial-cosmology-without-inflation}{%
\subsection{Appendix W -- Primordial Cosmology without
Inflation}\label{appendix-w-primordial-cosmology-without-inflation}}

\textbf{Note:} This appendix develops the speculative scenarios of
primordial cosmology mentioned in §9. For the main cosmological
discussion, see §9.1--§9.7.

\hypertarget{w.1-homogeneity-from-generalised-gauge-invariance}{%
\subsubsection{W.1 Homogeneity from generalised gauge
invariance}\label{w.1-homogeneity-from-generalised-gauge-invariance}}

In the Janus model, the early universe undergoes a generalised gauge
transformation where all physical constants vary coherently {[}27{]}.
The speed of light \(c\), the gravitational constant \(G\), and particle
masses scale as:

\[
c(t) \propto a(t), \quad G(t) \propto a(t)^2, \quad m(t) \propto a(t),
\]

where \(a(t)\) is the scale factor. This gauge invariance preserves the
form of all physical equations while ensuring that the cosmological
horizon grows with the universe, maintaining homogeneity at all scales.
No inflaton field is required. The transition occurs when the
inter-baryon distance falls below the Compton wavelength, triggering
this collective gauge evolution.

The following quantities vary simultaneously under this generalised
gauge transformation:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \(\bar{c}\) (speed of light)
\item
  \(\bar{G}\) (gravitational constant)
\item
  \(\bar{\hbar}\) (reduced Planck constant)
\item
  \(\bar{m}\) (particle masses)
\item
  \(\bar{a}\) (scale factor)
\end{itemize}

All other constants (fine-structure constant \(\alpha\), charge \(e\),
etc.) remain invariant. The horizon problem is resolved because the
cosmological horizon scales with the universe's expansion, maintaining
causal contact at all scales.

\hypertarget{w.2-cmb-fluctuations-as-gravitational-imprint-of-the-negative-sector}{%
\subsubsection{W.2 CMB fluctuations as gravitational imprint of the
negative
sector}\label{w.2-cmb-fluctuations-as-gravitational-imprint-of-the-negative-sector}}

The Jeans length in the negative-mass sector is approximately 100 times
larger than in the positive sector {[}28{]}:

\[
\frac{L_J^{(-)}}{L_J^{(+)}} \propto \frac{a^{(-)}}{a^{(+)}} \approx 100.
\]

Consequently, density fluctuations in the Ke sector have characteristic
angular scales of about one degree on the CMB sky. These fluctuations
gravitationally imprint onto the positive sector through the coupling
tensor \(\stackrel{\frown}{T}^{(-)}_{\mu\nu}\), generating the observed
CMB power spectrum without requiring primordial quantum fluctuations.
This prediction distinguishes Janus from \(\Lambda\)CDM and can be
tested with Planck data.

The temperature fluctuations \(\Delta T/T\) observed by Planck are thus
interpreted as the projection of negative-sector density contrasts:

\[
\frac{\Delta T}{T}(\hat{\mathbf{n}}) = \int_0^{z_{\text{rec}}} \Phi^{(-)}(r\hat{\mathbf{n}}, z) \, dz,
\]

where \(\Phi^{(-)}\) is the gravitational potential in the Ke sector.

\hypertarget{w.3-asymmetric-speed-of-light}{%
\subsubsection{W.3 Asymmetric speed of
light}\label{w.3-asymmetric-speed-of-light}}

From the gauge evolution equations, the ratio of light speeds in the two
sectors is {[}19{]}:

\[
\frac{c^{(-)}}{c^{(+)}} \propto \frac{a^{(+)}}{a^{(-)}} \approx 10.
\]

Light in the negative sector travels ten times faster than in our
sector. Combined with the Jeans length ratio
(\(L_J^{(-)}/L_J^{(+)} \approx 100\)), this reduces interstellar travel
times by a factor of 1000 if mass inversion could be achieved.

\textbf{Conjectured physical consequences:}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3810}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.6190}}@{}}
\toprule
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Effect
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Implication
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule
\endhead
Faster communication & Signals in Ke sector travel 10× faster \\
Larger Jeans length & Structures in Ke sector are 100× larger \\
Travel time reduction & Interstellar travel 1000× faster (if mass
inversion achieved) \\
\bottomrule
\end{longtable}

\hypertarget{w.4-relation-to-the-spectral-gap-delta_0}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{W.4 Relation to the spectral gap
\(\Delta_0\)}{W.4 Relation to the spectral gap \textbackslash Delta\_0}}\label{w.4-relation-to-the-spectral-gap-delta_0}}

The gauge evolution is triggered when the topological tension
\(\mathcal{T}\) exceeds the lattice minimal norm
\(\mu_{\Lambda_{72}} = 8\) (see §10.6.1). This condition is equivalent
to crossing the spectral threshold \(S_7\), which activates the octave
jump and initiates the gauge transformation. The value of
\(\Delta_0 = 2.5\)\,MeV is the energy scale at which this transition
occurs in the positive sector.

\hypertarget{w.5-open-questions}{%
\subsubsection{W.5 Open questions}\label{w.5-open-questions}}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  What determines the exact ratio \(c^{(-)}/c^{(+)} = 10\)? Is it
  related to the eigenvalues of \(\Lambda_{72}\)?
\item
  How does the gauge transition couple to the pentadic network?
\item
  Can the CMB power spectrum be quantitatively reproduced from the
  negative-sector density fluctuations?
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{appendix-x-bubble-universes-and-the-accessibility-of-the-big-bang}{%
\subsection{Appendix X -- Bubble Universes and the Accessibility of the
Big
Bang}\label{appendix-x-bubble-universes-and-the-accessibility-of-the-big-bang}}

\textbf{Note:} This appendix develops speculative scenarios mentioned in
§9. For the main cosmological discussion, see §9.1--§9.7.

\hypertarget{x.1-bubble-universes-with-different-constants}{%
\subsubsection{X.1 Bubble universes with different
constants}\label{x.1-bubble-universes-with-different-constants}}

In the Janus model, each void (bubble) in the large-scale structure may
have its own set of fundamental constants (\(c\), \(G\), \(\hbar\),
\(\alpha_{\text{em}}\)) inherited from the gauge evolution phase
{[}28{]}. However, the form of the physical equations is identical
across bubbles, ensuring similar evolutionary histories---galaxies,
stars, planets, and even biomolecules can form in each. This provides a
natural realisation of the ``baby universe'' scenario without
fine-tuning.

\textbf{Properties of bubble universes:}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4348}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.5652}}@{}}
\toprule
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Property
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Description
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule
\endhead
\textbf{Constants} & May vary between bubbles (\(c\), \(G\),
\(\hbar\)) \\
\textbf{Physics} & Same equations, different parameters \\
\textbf{Evolution} & Parallel histories (stars, galaxies, life) \\
\textbf{Communication} & No interaction between bubbles (different
\(g_{\mu\nu}\)) \\
\bottomrule
\end{longtable}

The variation of constants between bubbles is constrained by the
requirement that atomic physics remains functional for life to emerge.
This is a mild anthropic selection principle.

\hypertarget{x.2-cosmological-time-and-the-inaccessibility-of-the-big-bang}{%
\subsubsection{X.2 Cosmological time and the inaccessibility of the Big
Bang}\label{x.2-cosmological-time-and-the-inaccessibility-of-the-big-bang}}

In the Janus model with variable constants, an elementary clock (two
masses orbiting their common centre of gravity) sees its period \(T\)
tend to zero as one approaches the origin {[}23{]}:

\[
T(t) \propto a(t) \to 0 \quad \text{as} \quad t \to t_{\text{BB}}.
\]

Consequently, the clock completes an infinite number of rotations before
reaching the Big Bang. The origin is asymptotically inaccessible---a
realisation of Zeno's paradox at the cosmological scale. The question
``what happened before the Big Bang?'' loses its meaning because one
cannot operationally define ``before'' under these conditions.

\textbf{Diagrammatic representation:}

\begin{verbatim}
      Future
         ↑
         │
    ─────┼─────  Present
         │
    infinite number
    of rotations     Big Bang
    ─────────────────────────→ Time
    (asymptotically inaccessible)
\end{verbatim}

\hypertarget{x.3-relational-time-vs-absolute-time}{%
\subsubsection{X.3 Relational time vs absolute
time}\label{x.3-relational-time-vs-absolute-time}}

In this framework, time is not an absolute parameter but a
\textbf{relational quantity} defined by the number of rotations of an
elementary clock. The impossibility of reaching \(t=0\) reflects the
fact that relational time does not have a natural origin---it is defined
only up to an arbitrary reference point. This perspective aligns with
the relational philosophy underlying \(\text{Cl}(6,6)\) itself.

\hypertarget{x.4-connection-to-the-pentadic-network}{%
\subsubsection{X.4 Connection to the pentadic
network}\label{x.4-connection-to-the-pentadic-network}}

The infinite number of rotations before reaching the Big Bang
corresponds to the existence of an infinite sequence of pentadic
configurations as one approaches the spectral threshold \(S_7\) from
below. The topological tension \(\mathcal{T}\) diverges as
\(t \to t_{\text{BB}}\), preventing the system from ever reaching the
singular point.

\hypertarget{x.5-open-questions}{%
\subsubsection{X.5 Open questions}\label{x.5-open-questions}}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Is the infinite number of rotations a genuine physical prediction or a
  mathematical artefact?
\item
  How does this scenario relate to the bounce cosmology alternatives?
\item
  Can this be tested observationally (e.g., through signatures in the
  CMB)?
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{appendix-y-cultural-isomorphisms-and-ancestral-debts}{%
\subsection{Appendix Y -- Cultural Isomorphisms and Ancestral
Debts}\label{appendix-y-cultural-isomorphisms-and-ancestral-debts}}

\hypertarget{y.1-overview}{%
\subsubsection{Y.1 Overview}\label{y.1-overview}}

The \(64 \to 20\) reduction encoded in our transition operator \(T\) and
Merkabah filtration is not an isolated epistemic artifact. It appears as
a \textbf{topological invariant} whose complementary projections have
been articulated by distinct formal traditions across different
civilizations. Their convergence --- none derived from the others ---
validates the hypothesis of a universal constraint independent of
symbolic systems.

\hypertarget{y.2-the-chinese-tradition-combinatorial-prefiltering}{%
\subsubsection{Y.2 The Chinese tradition: combinatorial
pre‑filtering}\label{y.2-the-chinese-tradition-combinatorial-prefiltering}}

The \emph{Yi Jing} and \emph{Wu Xing} (Five Phases) model the
\textbf{phase of combinatorial pre‑filtering}. The 64 hexagrams
constitute an exhaustive binary configuration space strictly isomorphic
to the 6‑bit vectors of \(\mathrm{Cl}(6,0)\). The \emph{sheng}
(generative) and \emph{ke} (regulatory) cycles describe a five‑phase
local dynamic, corresponding to the internal regulation of attractor
states. This tradition formalizes the \textbf{geometry of possibilities}
and the rules of relational circulation, without postulating a priori a
fixed reduction to 20 functional classes.

\textbf{Correspondence table:}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}ll@{}}
\toprule
Yi Jing concept & Mathematical counterpart \\
\midrule
\endhead
64 hexagrams & Binary space \(\mathrm{Cl}(6,0)\) \\
Yin/Yang (\(--\)/\(-\)) & Bits 0/1 \\
Hexagram sequence & Time-ordered configurations \\
Wu Xing cycles & \(CP/CN\) tropical belts \\
\bottomrule
\end{longtable}

\hypertarget{y.3-the-hebrew-tradition-functional-postfiltering}{%
\subsubsection{Y.3 The Hebrew tradition: functional
post‑filtering}\label{y.3-the-hebrew-tradition-functional-postfiltering}}

The \emph{Sefer Yetzirah} operates explicitly at the level of
\textbf{post‑filtering}. The 22 consonantal letters (plus 5 final
\emph{sofit} forms) encode a functional partition of semantic space into
\textbf{20 stable classes plus 2 boundary states}. The letters
\emph{Aleph} (primordial breath / reference) and \emph{Tav} (signature /
closure) structurally overlap with the threshold roles of initiation and
termination in biological translation (methionine / STOP codons). The
canonical tripartition --- \textbf{3 mothers, 7 doubles, 12 singles} ---
discretizes the gradient of geometric constraints, directly reflecting
the polarity signatures (\(3P\), \(2P+1N\), \(1P+2N\), \(3N\)) resulting
from Merkabah filtration {[}9{]}.

This tripartition corresponds precisely to:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{3 mothers} → the 3 structural elements (\(e_1,e_2,e_3\))
\item
  \textbf{7 doubles} → the 7 spectral thresholds \(S_1,\ldots,S_7\)
\item
  \textbf{12 singles} → the 12 spectral partitions of
  \(\mathrm{Cl}(6,6)\), generating \(12 \times 12 = 144\) pentads
\end{itemize}

\hypertarget{y.4-mandarin-phonology-independent-confirmation}{%
\subsubsection{Y.4 Mandarin phonology: independent
confirmation}\label{y.4-mandarin-phonology-independent-confirmation}}

Although derived from a non‑alphabetic ideographic tradition, Mandarin
syllabic structure is organized around a consonantal onset system of
\textbf{21 initials} (often extended to 22 in educational
romanizations), coupled with a minimal vowel nucleus reduced to 2--3
fundamental phonemes. This phonological architecture (\textasciitilde22
consonantal anchors framing a restricted vowel nucleus) structurally
reflects the \textbf{20\,+\,2 partition}. It suggests that the
compression of combinatorial complexity into stable functional classes
emerges independently whenever transmission systems are constrained by
analogous articulatory, perceptual, and cognitive limits --- a principle
that extends from language to genetics (64 codons → 20 amino acids) and,
as we argue, to fundamental physics.

\hypertarget{y.5-the-two-faces-of-the-medal}{%
\subsubsection{Y.5 The two faces of the
medal}\label{y.5-the-two-faces-of-the-medal}}

These cultural formalisms are not superimposable; they are
\textbf{orthogonal projections} of the same topological invariant. The
Chinese tradition captures the \textbf{dynamics of transformation in
configuration space} (pre‑filtering). The Hebrew tradition formalizes
its \textbf{reduction to stable functional classes} and the definition
of limit states (post‑filtering). Their convergence --- independently
derived, without mutual influence --- validates the hypothesis of a
\textbf{universal constraint} independent of symbolic systems.

Remarkably, the same complementary structure appears in contemporary
physics. Jean‑Pierre Petit's \textbf{Janus cosmology} (macro‑scale,
bimetric coupling of positive and negative masses) and Peter Rowlands'
\textbf{nilpotent formalism} (micro‑scale, \((g\cdot x)^2=0\), Dirac
equation, spin‑½) are two faces of the same medal. Both are orthogonal
projections of the same algebraic substrate: \(\mathrm{Cl}(6,6)\).

\hypertarget{y.6-the-traditional-status-of-wu-xing-and-yi-jing-in-imperial-china}{%
\subsubsection{Y.6 The traditional status of Wu Xing and Yi Jing in
Imperial
China}\label{y.6-the-traditional-status-of-wu-xing-and-yi-jing-in-imperial-china}}

Historically, the \emph{Yi Jing} and \emph{Wu Xing} (Five Phases) were
integrated into the ideological foundation of the Chinese imperial state
from the Qin (221--207 BCE) up to the fall of the last emperor in 1924.
They functioned as a \textbf{universal correlative cosmology} governing
virtually every domain of imperial life:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Governance}: legitimation of dynastic cycles through the
  ``Five Virtues'' (\emph{wude}); theory of the ``Mandate of Heaven''
  (\emph{tianming})
\item
  \textbf{Law}: codification of punishments and rituals according to
  seasonal and elemental cycles
\item
  \textbf{Medicine}: foundation of traditional Chinese medicine via the
  five phases and yin‑yang
\item
  \textbf{Military strategy}: tactical principles (Sun Tzu), troop
  movements aligned with seasonal elements
\item
  \textbf{Architecture and urban planning}: orientation according to
  geomancy (\emph{feng shui})
\item
  \textbf{Agriculture and calendar}: regulation of planting and
  harvesting based on solar-lunar cycles
\item
  \textbf{Music and aesthetics}: five-tone scale, correspondence between
  musical notes and elements
\item
  \textbf{Philosophy and ethics}: correlative thinking between human
  virtues and cosmic forces
\end{itemize}

By contrast, the societies of the ancient Near East and Mediterranean
based their social order primarily on mythico‑historical narratives
(e.g., theogonies, epic genealogies, biblical revelation). This
difference in the \emph{social institutionalisation} of knowledge does
not affect the mathematical isomorphisms documented here, but it
illustrates the diverse cultural vectors through which combinatorial
invariants have been preserved.

\hypertarget{y.7-on-the-ancestral-debts-of-the-scientific-enterprise}{%
\subsubsection{Y.7 On the ancestral debts of the scientific
enterprise}\label{y.7-on-the-ancestral-debts-of-the-scientific-enterprise}}

The modern Western narrative of science often presents itself as a
\emph{tabula rasa}, a break with the past in which the scientist appears
as a \emph{novus homo} without debts to previous ways of knowing. This
work challenges that narrative.

The correspondences we have documented --- between the 3 mothers, 7
doubles and 12 simples of the \emph{Sefer Yetzirah} and the 3 structural
elements, 7 spectral thresholds and 12 partitions of
\(\mathrm{Cl}(6,6)\); between the 5 phases of the \emph{Wu Xing} and the
3‑1‑1 decomposition of each pentad; between the 64 hexagrams of the
\emph{Yi Jing} and the binary configuration space of
\(\mathrm{Cl}(6,0)\) --- are not mere analogies or pedagogical
metaphors. They are \textbf{structural isomorphisms} between ancient
combinatorial systems and the formal mathematics of a 21st‑century
unification model.

These isomorphisms do not imply that ancient sages anticipated Clifford
algebras or lattice theory. They suggest, rather, that certain
\textbf{relational invariants} --- ways of compressing combinatorial
complexity into stable functional classes --- have been independently
discovered, under different epistemic constraints, in different
civilisations and epochs. The mathematician or physicist who formalises
these invariants today does not create them \emph{ex nihilo}; he
recognises patterns that have been glimpsed, from other angles, for
millennia.

Acknowledging this debt is not a concession to obscurantism. It is an
act of intellectual honesty. It situates the scientific enterprise
within the long history of human attempts to grasp the structure of
reality --- a history in which the \emph{Sefer Yetzirah}, the \emph{Yi
Jing}, and the \emph{Wu Xing} are not relics, but early witnesses.

\hypertarget{y.8-no-claim-of-historical-influence}{%
\subsubsection{Y.8 No claim of historical
influence}\label{y.8-no-claim-of-historical-influence}}

No claim of historical influence is made. The ancient traditions did not
anticipate Clifford algebras or bimetric cosmology, nor did Petit and
Rowlands draw on the \emph{Sefer Yetzirah} or the \emph{Yi Jing}.
Rather, different epistemic pathways, operating under different
constraints and in different historical contexts, have converged on
\textbf{structurally isomorphic solutions} to the problem of compressing
combinatorial complexity into stable, functional categories --- whether
cognitive, linguistic, biological, or physical.

The mathematics of \(\mathrm{Cl}(6,6)\) provides the common language in
which these complementary projections can finally be seen as two aspects
of a single unified substrate. This work is neither a proof of ancient
wisdom nor a validation of modern physics by tradition. It is a
\textbf{retrospective recognition} that the same relational invariants
--- the same ``faces of the medal'' --- have been glimpsed, from
different angles, across millennia and civilizations.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\textbf{Remaining challenges for future work:}

\begin{enumerate}

  Compute \(\Delta_0\) rigorously from the discrete Laplacian on
  \(\Lambda_{72}\)
\item

  operator \(T\)
\item

  \(\text{gap}_c\), \(z_0\)) from first principles via Boltzmann
  integration
\item
  Prove the spectral partition into 12 leaves from the representation

\end{enumerate}
